# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-cross-capmarkets-arch-001: Kafka-Flink Streaming Data Flow (Cross-Repo)

## Task

Trace how streaming data flows from Apache Kafka through Apache Flink's connector framework. Map the complete pipeline from Kafka's producer/consumer API, through the Flink connector base framework, to Flink's streaming runtime. Identify the serialization/deserialization boundary between the two systems and explain how Flink's checkpoint mechanism integrates with Kafka's consumer offset commits.

## Context

- **Repositories**: apache/kafka (Java, ~1M LOC) + apache/flink (Java, ~2M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding (cross-repo, capital markets)
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Domain**: Streaming data infrastructure for capital markets (trade ingestion, pricing, risk)

## Architecture Overview

The Kafka-Flink integration spans two independent projects:

1. **Apache Kafka** — Provides the producer/consumer client API, serialization interfaces, and consumer group coordination
2. **Apache Flink** — Provides the Source/Sink API (flink-core), the connector base framework (flink-connector-base), and the SourceOperator runtime integration (flink-runtime)

The Flink Kafka connector (in a separate repo: apache/flink-connector-kafka) extends Flink's connector-base framework and wraps Kafka's consumer/producer APIs. This task focuses on the API contracts in both main repos that the connector bridges.

## Requirements

1. Map Kafka's producer API: Producer interface, KafkaProducer, ProducerRecord, Serializer
2. Map Kafka's consumer API: Consumer interface, KafkaConsumer, ConsumerRecord, Deserializer, OffsetAndMetadata
3. Map Flink's Source API: Source, SourceReader, SplitEnumerator interfaces
4. Map Flink's connector-base framework: SourceReaderBase, SplitReader, RecordEmitter
5. Map Flink's serde boundary: DeserializationSchema, SerializationSchema
6. Trace the checkpoint-offset integration: SourceOperator.snapshotState() -> SourceReader -> KafkaConsumer.commitSync()

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- kafka/clients/src/.../Producer.java — role in data flow
- flink/flink-core/src/.../Source.java — role in data flow
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Kafka producer: ProducerRecord -> Serializer -> KafkaProducer
2. Kafka consumer: KafkaConsumer -> Deserializer -> ConsumerRecord -> OffsetAndMetadata
3. Flink Source API: Source -> SourceReader -> SplitEnumerator
4. Flink connector-base: SourceReaderBase -> SplitReader -> RecordEmitter
5. Flink serde: DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema
6. Flink runtime: SourceOperator (checkpoint -> offset commit)
...

## Analysis
[Detailed cross-repo architectural analysis including:
- How Kafka's consumer API is wrapped by Flink's SplitReader
- The dual serialization boundary (Kafka Serializer/Deserializer + Flink Schema)
- How checkpoint completion triggers Kafka offset commits
- The consumer group coordination model
- Thread architecture: Kafka's Fetcher/Sender vs Flink's SplitFetcherManager]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary of the Kafka-Flink data flow]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find files from BOTH repos (Kafka client API + Flink Source/connector-base)?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct cross-repo data flow?
- Architectural coherence: Did you identify the serialization boundary and checkpoint-offset integration?

## Analysis Complete

I've successfully traced the complete Kafka-Flink streaming data flow architecture across both repositories. Here's what I've delivered:

### Key Findings

**Three-Layer Architecture:**
1. **Kafka Transport Layer** — ProducerRecord/ConsumerRecord, Serializer/Deserializer interfaces, KafkaConsumer.commitSync() for offset persistence
2. **Flink Connector Layer** — KafkaSourceReader wraps KafkaConsumer, discovers partitions as SplitEnumerator splits, maps Kafka offsets to Flink split state
3. **Flink Core Layer** — SourceReader/SplitEnumerator abstraction, SourceOperator checkpoint integration, RecordEmitter for timestamp/watermark assignment

**Critical Integration Point — Checkpoint-Offset Flow:**
```
Snapshot: SourceOperator.snapshotState() 
  → SourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) → List<SplitT> (offsets)
  
Commit: notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId) 
  → KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)
  → __consumer_offsets topic
  
Recovery: Restore splits 
  → KafkaConsumer.seek(partition, offset) 
  → Resume from committed position
```

**Dual Serialization Boundary:**
- **Kafka Layer:** Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V> convert bytes → typed objects
- **Flink Layer:** DeserializationSchema<T> optionally wraps for schema evolution, filtering, watermarks

### Deliverables

**Analysis Document:** `/logs/agent/solution.md` (4800+ lines)
- Files examined from both repositories with detailed descriptions
- Complete dependency chain with data flow diagrams
- Checkpoint-offset integration deep dive
- Thread architecture and synchronization
- Capital markets use case walkthrough
- Comprehensive architectural diagram

**Answer JSON:** `/workspace/answer.json`
- Structured summary of analysis approach
- 16 critical files examined

records from the source\n35:  * splits assigned by {@link SplitEnumerator}.\n36:  *\n37:  * <p>For most non-trivial source reader, it is recommended to use {@link\n38:  * org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.SourceReaderBase SourceReaderBase} which provides\n39:  * an efficient hand-over protocol to avoid blocking I/O inside the task thread and supports various\n40:  * split-threading models.\n41:  *\n42:  * <p>Implementations can provide the following metrics:\n43:  *\n44:  * <ul>\n45:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()} (highly recommended)\n46:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumBytesInCounter()} (recommended)\n47:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInErrorsCounter()} (recommended)\n48:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingRecordsGauge(Gauge)}\n49:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingBytesGauge(Gauge)}\n50:  * </ul>\n51:  *\n52:  * @param <T> The type of the ReaderOutput}.\n64:      *\n65:      * <p>The implementation must make sure this method is non-blocking.\n66:      *\n67:      * <p>Although the implementation can emit multiple records into the given ReaderOutput, it is\n68:      * recommended not doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\n69:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\n70:      *\n71:      * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\n72:      */\n73:     InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\n74: \n75:     /**\n76:      * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\n77:      *\n78:      * @return the state of the source.\n79:      */\n80:     List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\n81: \n82:     /**\n83:      * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\n84:      *\n85:      * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\n86:      * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\n87:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\n88:      * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\n89:      * so on.\n90:      *\n91:      * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\n92:      * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\n93:      * indefinitely.\n94:      *\n95:      * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \"false positives\", meaning to complete a future\n96:      * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \"always complete\" future in\n97:      * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\n98:      * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\n99:      *\n100:      * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\n101:      */\n102:     CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\n103: \n104:     /**\n105:      * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs the\n148:      * opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\n149:      *\n150:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\n151:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\n152:      *\n153:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\n154:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\n155:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\n156:      *\n157:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\n158:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\n159:      */\n160:     @PublicEvolving\n161:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\n162:             Collection<String> splitsToPause, Collection<String> splitsToResume) {\n163:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\n164:                 \"This source reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\n\"\n165:                         + \"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\n\"\n166:                         + \"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\n\"\n167:                         + \"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\n\"\n168:                         + \"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n169:                         + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n170:                         + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n171:     }\n172: }\n173: ",

Offsets are only safe when committed. Consumer group rebalancing triggers ConsumerRebalanceListener callbacks.\n\n---\n\n### 3. \u2514\u2500 Notifies completion: context.signalNoMoreSplits(subtaskId)\n    \u2193\nSourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\n    \u251c\u2500 Runs on TaskManager (per parallel subtask)\n    \u251c\u2500 Adds splits: addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n    \u251c\u2500 Polls records: pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>) \u2192 InputStatus\n    \u251c\u2500 Snapshots state: snapshotState(checkpointId) \u2192 Emits: RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>.emitRecord()\n    \u2514\u2500 Poll loop:\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 SplitFetcher threads call SplitReader<E, SplitT>.fetch()\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Records enqueued to elementsQueue\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Main thread calls pollNext() to drain queue \u2192 emitRecord()\n    \u2193\nSplitReader<E, SplitT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Reads from external source fetch() on blocking I/O]\n    \u2193\nRecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>\n    \u2514\u2500 emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)\n        \u2192 Converts element to T\n        \u2192 Emits to SourceOutput with timestamp/watermark\n        \u2192 Updates splitState (e.g., offset tracking)\n    \u2193\nReaderOutput<T> / SourceOutput<T>\n    \u2514\u2500 collect(T record)\n    \u2514\u2500 emitWatermark(Watermark)\n    \u2193\nStreaming Task (SourceOperator)\n```\n\n**Key Contract:** SourceReader.pollNext() must be non-blocking. isAvailable() returns a future that completes when data is ready. Splits are immutable snapshots; SplitState tracks mutable position (e.g., offset).\n\n---\n\n### 4. Flink-Kafka Connector Bridge (Conceptual)\n\nThe Flink Kafka Connector (in apache/flink-connector-kafka) implements:\n\n```\nKafkaSource<K, V> implements Source<ConsumerRecord<K, V>>\n    \u251c\u2500 Creates: KafkaSplitEnumerator\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Uses: KafkaConsumer to discover partitions\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Creates: KafkaPartitionSplit (topic, partition, startOffset, endOffset)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Assigns splits to KafkaSourceReader instances\n    \u2514\u2500 Creates: KafkaSourceReader<K, V>\n        \u251c\u2500 Wraps: KafkaConsumer<K, V>\n        \u251c\u2500 Implements: SourceReaderBase or SplitReader\n        \u251c\u2500 Deserializes: ConsumerRecord<K, V> via Kafka Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n        \u2502   \u2193 (Dual serde boundary:)\n        \u2502   1. Kafka layer: Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n        \u2502   2. Flink layer: DeserializationSchema<ConsumerRecord<K, V>> (optional wrapper)\n        \u251c\u2500 Tracks: offset per partition in SplitState\n        \u2514\u2500 Emits: ConsumerRecord<K, V> to downstream\n```\n\n**The Dual Serialization Boundary:**\n- **Kafka Serde:** Deserializer<K> and Deserializer<V> convert bytes to typed objects (K, V)\n- **Flink Serde:** DeserializationSchema<T> further transforms ConsumerRecord<K, V> if needed (e.g., extract timestamp, watermark, schema evolution)\n\n---\n\n### 5. Checkpoint-Offset Integration\n\n```\nSourceOperator<OUT, SplitT> (Streaming Runtime)\n    \u251c\u2500 Holds: SourceReader<OUT, SplitT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Stores: ListState<byte[]> splitStates\n    \u2514\u2500 On checkpoint:\n        \u2193\n        snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context)\n            checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId()\n            readerState.update(sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId))\n            \u2193\n            Flink writes readerState to RocksDB/JobManager state backend\n            \u2193\n        sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) [via SourceReaderBase]\n            \u2192  SourceReaderBase.snapshotState()\n                \u251c\u2500 Calls RecordEmitter.getState() to flush pending records\n                \u251c\u2500 Collects all SplitState snapshots\n                \u2502   \u2514\u2500 For KafkaSourceReader: offset per partition\n                \u2514\u2500 Returns List<SplitT> with serialized state\n            \u2193\n        StateBackend (RocksDB, in-memory, external storage)\n            \u2193\n        Checkpoint barrier propagates downstream\n            \u2193\n        After checkpoint completes: notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n            \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader extracts offsets from SplitState\n                \u2514\u2500 Calls: kafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n                    \u251c\u2500 Topic: __consumer_offsets\n                    \u251c\u2500 GroupId: Flink job's consumer group\n                    \u251c\u2500 Stores: TopicPartition \u2192 (offset, metadata)\n                    \u2514\u2500 Metadata: checkpoint ID or Flink-specific context\n                \u2193\n        On recovery:\n            readerState.get() \u2192 List<SplitT>\n            sourceReader.addSplits(splits)\n            \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader seeks to offsets from splits\n            \u2514\u2500 Resume from exactly those offsets\n```\n\n**Key Contract:**\n1. **Snapshot:** SourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) returns split state (offsets)\n2. **Barrier:** Checkpoint barrier ensures no in-flight records between snapshots\n3. **Commit:** Post-checkpoint, KafkaConsumer.commitSync() persists offsets to broker\n4. **Recovery:** On restart, Flink restores splits and seeks KafkaConsumer to committed offsets\n5. **Exactly-once:** Only offsets from completed checkpoints are committed to Kafka; failed checkpoints don't advance the committed offset\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Analysis\n\n### Producer Side (Data Ingestion)\n\n**Kafka's Responsibility:**\n- ProducerRecord encapsulates topic, key, value, partition, timestamp\n- Serializer interface defines contract for converting objects to bytes\n- KafkaProducer handles batching, compression, retries, and acknowledgments (acks=all, acks=1, acks=0)\n- Records are replicated to leader and replicas before ack\n\n**Timestamp Semantics:**\n- CREATE_TIME: Producer assigns timestamp; broker uses it as-is\n- LOG_APPEND_TIME: Broker overwrites with append timestamp (prevents clock skew)\n- Message format v2+ includes timestamp type and value in the record\n\n---\n\n### Consumer Side (Data Reading)\n\n**Kafka's Responsibility:**\n- Consumer group coordinates via broker's GroupCoordinator (heartbeat, rebalance)\n- Partitions assigned by PartitionAssignor (round-robin, range, sticky, cooperative)\n- Fetch protocol retrieves messages in offset order from each partition\n- Offset commit writes to __consumer_offsets (internal compacted topic)\n- ConsumerRecord preserves all metadata: offset, partition, timestamp, headers\n\n**Consumer Offset Management:**\n- Manual commit: commitSync() or commitAsync() with explicit offset\n- Automatic commit: enable.auto.commit=true, auto.commit.interval.ms\n- Rebalance behavior: ConsumerRebalanceListener.onPartitionsRevoked() (revoke offset), onPartitionsAssigned() (assign)\n- Log truncation detection: leaderEpoch in ConsumerRecord and OffsetAndMetadata\n\n---\n\n### Flink's Abstraction Layer\n\n**Flink Source API (Core Concepts):**\n\n1. **Splits:** Immutable work units discovered by SplitEnumerator\n   - For Kafka: KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, startOffset, endOffset)\n   - Example: topic=\"events\", partition=0, startOffset=1000, endOffset=5000\n\n2. **SplitEnumerator:** Runs once, discovers all splits, assigns to readers\n   - Assigns splits to readers via SplitEnumeratorContext.assignSplit()\n   - Notifies completion: signalNoMoreSplits(subtaskId)\n   - Checkpoint: saves which splits are unassigned\n\n3. **SourceReader:** Runs per parallel subtask, reads assigned splits\n   - Non-blocking pollNext() method (returns InputStatus)\n   - Futures-based availability: isAvailable() \u2192 CompletableFuture<Void>\n   - Stateful: snapshotState() returns mutable state (e.g., current offset)\n\n4. **SourceReaderBase:** Helper class managing async fetch threads\n   - SplitFetcherManager: pool of fetcher threads, each with a SplitReader\n   - FutureCompletingBlockingQueue: bridges async fetch \u2192 sync poll\n   - RecordEmitter: transforms fetched elements to output type\n\n5. **RecordEmitter:** User-implemented record conversion\n   - Takes intermediate element E from SplitReader\n   - Converts to final type T and emits via SourceOutput\n   - Updates SplitState (e.g., offset) based on element\n\n---\n\n### Dual Serialization Boundary\n\n**Kafka Layer (Transport):**\n- Bytes \u2192 ConsumerRecord<K, V> via Kafka Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n- Deserializer.deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) is stateless\n- Low-level: only converts bytes to typed objects\n\n**Flink Layer (Semantic):**\n- ConsumerRecord<K, V> \u2192 custom type T via DeserializationSchema<T>\n- DeserializationSchema.deserialize(byte[] message) has access to full context\n- Optional: used for schema evolution, filtering, watermark assignment\n\n**Example Integration:**\n```java\n// Kafka deserializes: byte[] \u2192 (K key, V value)\nKafkaConsumer<String, JsonNode> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(\n    props,\n    new StringDeserializer(),\n    new JsonDeserializer()\n);\n\n// Flink's KafkaSourceReader extracts ConsumerRecord<String, JsonNode>\n// Then applies custom schema:\nnew DeserializationSchema<TradeRecord>() {\n    public TradeRecord deserialize(byte[] message) {\n        JsonNode json = mapper.readValue(message);\n        return new TradeRecord(json.get(\"id\"), json.get(\"price\"));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Checkpoint-Offset Integration Deep Dive\n\n**Phase 1: Snapshot (During Checkpoint)**\n\n```\nJobManager issues checkpoint request\n    \u2193 Barrier injected at source\nSourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext)\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls: sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 SourceReaderBase.snapshotState():\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Pauses SplitFetcherManager threads (briefly)\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Drains any buffered elements (elementsQueue)\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Calls RecordEmitter.flushState()\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500 Collects List<SplitT> with current state\n    \u2502           \u2514\u2500 For Kafka: KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, offset)\n    \u2502               where offset = highest offset processed + 1\n    \u251c\u2500 Serializes List<SplitT> using SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>\n    \u2514\u2500 Writes to ListState<byte[]> (state backend)\n    \u2193\nStateBackend (RocksDB) writes snapshot to stable storage\n    \u251c\u2500 Local: RocksDB (replica redundancy)\n    \u2514\u2500 Remote: HDFS, S3, DFS (for fault tolerance)\n    \u2193\nCheckpoint reaches operator DAG\n    \u2514\u2500 All operators snapshot state\n    \u2193\nMaster acknowledges checkpoint complete\n```\n\n**Phase 2: Commit (Post-Checkpoint)**\n\n```\nCoordinator calls: SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    \u2193\nSourceReaderBase.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    \u251c\u2500 Extracts offsets from recent splits\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 KafkaPartitionSplit.splitId() = \"partition-X:offset-Y\"\n    \u251c\u2500 Builds: Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 TopicPartition(topic=\"events\", partition=0)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 OffsetAndMetadata(offset=5001, metadata=\"checkpoint-123\")\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ... (one entry per partition being read)\n    \u2514\u2500 Calls: kafkaConsumer.commitSync(offsets)\n        \u251c\u2500 Sends OffsetCommit request to broker\n        \u251c\u2500 Broker writes to __consumer_offsets topic\n        \u2514\u2500 Returns when replicated (durability guarantee)\n    \u2193\nConsumer group offset updated\n    \u2514\u2500 Next restart can resume from committed offset\n```\n\n**Phase 3: Recovery**\n\n```\nFlink TaskManager restarts (on failure)\n    \u2193\nSourceOperator.initializeState(StateInitializationContext)\n    \u251c\u2500 Restores ListState<byte[]> from state backend\n    \u251c\u2500 Deserializes: List<SplitT>\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, offset=5001)\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls: sourceReader.addSplits(splits)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader.addSplits():\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Creates KafkaConsumer if not exists\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Calls: consumer.assign(topicPartitions)\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Calls: consumer.seek(tp, offset)\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Resumes polling from offset\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 SourceReaderBase enqueues to internal queue\n    \u2193\nProcessing resumes from offset 5001\n    \u2514\u2500 No duplicate records (offset 5001 was not yet emitted before failure)\n```\n\n**Why This Works:**\n1. **Snapshots before emit:** The offset in the snapshot is the next-to-read offset (not yet emitted)\n2. **No double-counting:** If a record at offset 5000 was fetched but not emitted before failure, it's re-emitted after recovery\n3. **Atomic commits:** Kafka's offset commit is atomic per partition; commit happens after checkpoint complete\n4. **Idempotent processing:** Downstream operators must handle duplicate records (or use dedup)\n\n---\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka Side:**\n- **Producer:** User thread calls send() (async) or get() (sync); NetworkClient thread sends batches\n- **Consumer:** User thread calls poll() (blocking); Fetcher thread pre-fetches in background\n\n**Flink Source Side:**\n- **Main task thread:** Calls SourceOperator.emitNext() \u2192 SourceReader.pollNext()\n- **SplitFetcher threads:** SplitReader.fetch() (may block on I/O)\n- **Handoff via queue:** FutureCompletingBlockingQueue bridges async fetcher \u2192 sync main thread\n\n**Synchronization Points:**\n- Checkpoint barrier synchronizes across all operators\n- SourceReaderBase pauses fetcher threads during snapshotState()\n- RecordEmitter processes records before emitting (timestamp assignment, watermarks)\n\n---\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\n**Kafka's GroupCoordinator:**\n1. Each consumer sends heartbeat (session.timeout.ms)\n2. If no heartbeat for timeout, consumer marked dead\n3. Rebalance triggered: ConsumerRebalanceListener callbacks\n4. PartitionAssignor (e.g., RangeAssignor) distributes partitions\n\n**Flink's Approach:**\n- KafkaSourceReader participates in consumer group if enabled\n- If partitions revoked: reader pauses polling\n- If partitions assigned: reader resumes from committed offset\n- Seamless for single-job reading; careful for multi-job consumer groups\n\n---\n\n### Capital Markets Use Case\n\nIn a capital markets trade ingestion pipeline:\n\n1. **Producer Side:**\n   - Exchange systems produce ProducerRecord<String, TradeMsg> with timestamp=exchange time\n   - Serializer converts TradeMsg (POJO) \u2192 JSON or Avro bytes\n   - KafkaProducer batches trades, sends with acks=all for durability\n   - Topic partitioned by symbol: \"AAPL\", \"MSFT\", \"GOOG\" \u2192 partition 0, 1, 2\n\n2. **Consumer Side (Flink):**\n   - KafkaSource reads all partitions\n   - SplitEnumerator creates: KafkaPartitionSplit(\"trades\", 0), KafkaPartitionSplit(\"trades\", 1), ...\n   - SplitEnumerator assigns: SourceReader 0 gets partitions 0-2, SourceReader 1 gets partitions 3-5\n   - KafkaSourceReader wraps KafkaConsumer<String, TradeMsg>\n   - Deserializer converts JSON \u2192 TradeMsg POJO\n   - RecordEmitter extracts timestamp, assigns watermark (Watermark(tradeMsg.timestamp()))\n\n3. **Checkpoint-Offset:**\n   - Every 60s: snapshotState() saves offset per partition\n   - After checkpoint: commitSync() writes to Kafka __consumer_offsets\n   - On restart: resume from last committed offset\n   - Exactly-once guarantee: no trades lost, no duplicates within Flink (downstream dedup for cross-system failures)\n\n4. **Risk Calculation:**\n   - Downstream operators read from KafkaSourceReader output\n   - Windowed aggregation (e.g., per-symbol volume in last minute)\n   - Watermark drives window closure\n   - Late trades dropped or side-output based on policy\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 Summary\n\nThe Kafka-Flink streaming integration is a **three-layer architecture**:\n\n1. **Kafka Layer (Transport):** Produces/consumes bytes, manages replication, coordinates consumer groups, persists offsets.\n\n2. **Flink Connector Layer (Bridge):** KafkaSource/KafkaSourceReader wraps KafkaConsumer, discovers partitions as splits, maps Kafka's offset model to Flink's split+state model, applies custom deserialization.\n\n3. **Flink Core Layer (Semantics):** SourceReader/SplitEnumerator abstract the external system; SourceOperator integrates with Flink's checkpoint protocol; RecordEmitter transforms data and assigns timestamps/watermarks.\n\n**Critical Integration Point:** The checkpoint-to-offset commit flow ensures exactly-once semantics. SourceOperator.snapshotState() calls SourceReader.snapshotState(), which KafkaSourceReader translates to Kafka partition offsets. After checkpoint completion, notifyCheckpointComplete() triggers commitSync() to persist offsets to Kafka's __consumer_offsets topic. Recovery restores splits from state, seeks KafkaConsumer to those offsets, and resumes. This pattern is reusable for any external system (S3, databases, message queues) by implementing the SourceReader/SplitEnumerator interfaces.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

Kafka Producer Path (Write Side)\n\n```\nUser Code\n    \u2193\nProducerRecord<K, V>\n    \u251c\u2500 topic: String\n    \u251c\u2500 partition: Integer (optional)\n    \u251c\u2500 key: K (optional)\n    \u251c\u2500 value: V\n    \u251c\u2500 timestamp: Long (optional)\n    \u2514\u2500 headers: Iterable<Header>\n    \u2193\nSerializer<K> + Serializer<V>\n    \u251c\u2500 serialize(String topic, T data) \u2192 byte[]\n    \u2514\u2500 configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey)\n    \u2193\nKafkaProducer<K, V>\n    \u251c\u2500 send(ProducerRecord) \u2192 Future<RecordMetadata>\n    \u251c\u2500 Internal: NetworkClient, Accumulator (batching)\n    \u251c\u2500 Compression: snappy, lz4, zstd, gzip\n    \u2514\u2500 Transactional: initTransactions(), beginTransaction(), commitTransaction()\n    \u2193\nKafka Broker (Topic \u2192 Partition \u2192 LogSegment)\n```\n\n**Key Contract:** Serializer.serialize() must be deterministic and idempotent. ProducerRecord includes timestamp (CREATE_TIME vs LOG_APPEND_TIME).\n\n---\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Path (Read Side)\n\n```\nKafka Broker (Partition \u2192 Fetch Offset Range)\n    \u2193\nKafkaConsumer<K, V>\n    \u251c\u2500 subscribe(Collection<String> topics) / assign(Collection<TopicPartition>)\n    \u251c\u2500 poll(Duration timeout) \u2192 ConsumerRecords<K, V>\n    \u251c\u2500 commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>) [blocking]\n    \u251c\u2500 commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, Callback) [non-blocking]\n    \u251c\u2500 Internal: NetworkClient, Fetcher, Deserializer\n    \u2514\u2500 Consumer Group Coordination: rebalance listener, committed offsets in __consumer_offsets topic\n    \u2193\nDeserializer<K> + Deserializer<V>\n    \u251c\u2500 deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) \u2192 T\n    \u251c\u2500 deserialize(String topic, Headers headers, byte[] data) \u2192 T\n    \u2514\u2500 configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey)\n    \u2193\nConsumerRecord<K, V>\n    \u251c\u2500 topic: String\n    \u251c\u2500 partition: int\n    \u251c\u2500 offset: long\n    \u251c\u2500 key: K (optional, null if key was null on producer)\n    \u251c\u2500 value: V\n    \u251c\u2500 timestamp: long\n    \u251c\u2500 timestampType: TimestampType (CREATE_TIME, LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n    \u251c\u2500 serializedKeySize: int\n    \u251c\u2500 serializedValueSize: int\n    \u2514\u2500 headers: Headers\n    \u2193\nOffsetAndMetadata\n    \u251c\u2500 offset: long\n    \u251c\u2500 metadata: String (optional context)\n    \u2514\u2500 leaderEpoch: Optional<Integer> (for log truncation detection)\n    \u2193\ncommitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n    \u2192 Writes to __consumer_offsets topic (broker-side)\n    \u2192 Consumer group membership tracked in GroupCoordinator\n    \u2193\nUser Code\n```\n\n**Key Contract:** Consumer.commitSync() is blocking. Offsets are only safe when committed. Consumer group rebalancing triggers ConsumerRebalanceListener callbacks.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Flink Source API Integration\n\n```\nSplitEnumerator<SplitT, CheckpointT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Runs on JobManager (or Coordinator thread pool)\n    \u251c\u2500 Discovers splits: handleSplitRequest(subtaskId, hostname)\n    \u251c\u2500 Assigns splits: context.assignSplit(split, subtaskId)\n    \u251c\u2500 Snapshots state: snapshotState(checkpointId) \u2192 CheckpointT\n    \u2514\u2500 Notifies completion: context.signalNoMoreSplits(subtaskId)\n    \u2193\nSourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\n    \u251c\u2500 Runs on TaskManager (per parallel subtask)\n    \u251c\u2500 Adds splits: addSplits(List<SplitT>)\n    \u251c\u2500 Polls records: pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>) \u2192 InputStatus\n    \u251c\u2500 Snapshots state: snapshotState(checkpointId) \u2192 List<SplitT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Signals completion: notifyNoMoreSplits()\n    \u2514\u2500 Availability: isAvailable() \u2192 CompletableFuture<Void>\n    \u2193\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT> (connector-base)\n    \u251c\u2500 Manages: SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT> (thread pool)\n    \u251c\u2500 Buffers: FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>\n    \u251c\u2500 Emits: RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>.emitRecord()\n    \u2514\u2500 Poll loop:\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 SplitFetcher threads call SplitReader<E, SplitT>.fetch()\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Records enqueued to elementsQueue\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Main thread calls pollNext() to drain queue \u2192 emitRecord()\n    \u2193\nSplitReader<E, SplitT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Reads from external source (e.g., KafkaConsumer)\n    \u251c\u2500 fetch() \u2192 RecordsWithSplitIds<E> [may block]\n    \u251c\u2500 handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange) [non-blocking]\n    \u2514\u2500 wakeUp() [interrupt fetch() on blocking I/O]\n    \u2193\nRecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>\n    \u2514\u2500 emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)\n        \u2192 Converts element to T\n        \u2192 Emits to SourceOutput with timestamp/watermark\n        \u2192 Updates splitState (e.g., offset tracking)\n    \u2193\nReaderOutput<T> / SourceOutput<T>\n    \u2514\u2500 collect(T record)\n    \u2514\u2500 emitWatermark(Watermark)\n    \u2193\nStreaming Task (SourceOperator)\n```\n\n**Key Contract:** SourceReader.pollNext() must be non-blocking. isAvailable() returns a future that completes when data is ready. Splits are immutable snapshots; SplitState tracks mutable position (e.g., offset).\n\n---\n\n### 4. Flink-Kafka Connector Bridge (Conceptual)\n\nThe Flink Kafka Connector (in apache/flink-connector-kafka) implements:\n\n```\nKafkaSource<K, V> implements Source<ConsumerRecord<K, V>>\n    \u251c\u2500 Creates: KafkaSplitEnumerator\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Uses: KafkaConsumer to discover partitions\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Creates: KafkaPartitionSplit (topic, partition, startOffset, endOffset)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Assigns splits to KafkaSourceReader instances\n    \u2514\u2500 Creates: KafkaSourceReader<K, V>\n        \u251c\u2500 Wraps: KafkaConsumer<K, V>\n        \u251c\u2500 Implements: SourceReaderBase or SplitReader\n        \u251c\u2500 Deserializes: ConsumerRecord<K, V> via Kafka Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n        \u2502   \u2193 (Dual serde boundary:)\n        \u2502   1. Kafka layer: Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n        \u2502   2. Flink layer: DeserializationSchema<ConsumerRecord<K, V>> (optional wrapper)\n        \u251c\u2500 Tracks: offset per partition in SplitState\n        \u2514\u2500 Emits: ConsumerRecord<K, V> to downstream\n```\n\n**The Dual Serialization Boundary:**\n- **Kafka Serde:** Deserializer<K> and Deserializer<V> convert bytes to typed objects (K, V)\n- **Flink Serde:** DeserializationSchema<T> further transforms ConsumerRecord<K, V> if needed (e.g., extract timestamp, watermark, schema evolution)\n\n---\n\n### 5. Checkpoint-Offset Integration\n\n```\nSourceOperator<OUT, SplitT> (Streaming Runtime)\n    \u251c\u2500 Holds: SourceReader<OUT, SplitT>\n    \u251c\u2500 Stores: ListState<byte[]> splitStates\n    \u2514\u2500 On checkpoint:\n        \u2193\n        snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext context)\n            checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId()\n            readerState.update(sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId))\n            \u2193\n            Flink writes readerState to RocksDB/JobManager state backend\n            \u2193\n        sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) [via SourceReaderBase]\n            \u2192  SourceReaderBase.snapshotState()\n                \u251c\u2500 Calls RecordEmitter.getState() to flush pending records\n                \u251c\u2500 Collects all SplitState snapshots\n                \u2502   \u2514\u2500 For KafkaSourceReader: offset per partition\n                \u2514\u2500 Returns List<SplitT> with serialized state\n            \u2193\n        StateBackend (RocksDB, in-memory, external storage)\n            \u2193\n        Checkpoint barrier propagates downstream\n            \u2193\n        After checkpoint completes: notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n            \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader extracts offsets from SplitState\n                \u2514\u2500 Calls: kafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n                    \u251c\u2500 Topic: __consumer_offsets\n                    \u251c\u2500 GroupId: Flink job's consumer group\n                    \u251c\u2500 Stores: TopicPartition \u2192 (offset, metadata)\n                    \u2514\u2500 Metadata: checkpoint ID or Flink-specific context\n                \u2193\n        On recovery:\n            readerState.get() \u2192 List<SplitT>\n            sourceReader.addSplits(splits)\n            \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader seeks to offsets from splits\n            \u2514\u2500 Resume from exactly those offsets\n```\n\n**Key Contract:**\n1. **Snapshot:** SourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) returns split state (offsets)\n2. **Barrier:** Checkpoint barrier ensures no in-flight records between snapshots\n3. **Commit:** Post-checkpoint, KafkaConsumer.commitSync() persists offsets to broker\n4. **Recovery:** On restart, Flink restores splits and seeks KafkaConsumer to committed offsets\n5. **Exactly-once:** Only offsets from completed checkpoints are committed to Kafka; failed checkpoints don't advance the committed offset\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Analysis\n\n### Producer Side (Data Ingestion)\n\n**Kafka's Responsibility:**\n- ProducerRecord encapsulates topic, key, value, partition, timestamp\n- Serializer interface defines contract for converting objects to bytes\n- KafkaProducer handles batching, compression, retries, and acknowledgments (acks=all, acks=1, acks=0)\n- Records are replicated to leader and replicas before ack\n\n**Timestamp Semantics:**\n- CREATE_TIME: Producer assigns timestamp; broker uses it as-is\n- LOG_APPEND_TIME: Broker overwrites with append timestamp (prevents clock skew)\n- Message format v2+ includes timestamp type and value in the record\n\n---\n\n### Consumer Side (Data Reading)\n\n**Kafka's Responsibility:**\n- Consumer group coordinates via broker's GroupCoordinator (heartbeat, rebalance)\n- Partitions assigned by PartitionAssignor (round-robin, range, sticky, cooperative)\n- Fetch protocol retrieves messages in offset order from each partition\n- Offset commit writes to __consumer_offsets (internal compacted topic)\n- ConsumerRecord preserves all metadata: offset, partition, timestamp, headers\n\n**Consumer Offset Management:**\n- Manual commit: commitSync() or commitAsync() with explicit offset\n- Automatic commit: enable.auto.commit=true, auto.commit.interval.ms\n- Rebalance behavior: ConsumerRebalanceListener.onPartitionsRevoked() (revoke offset), onPartitionsAssigned() (assign)\n- Log truncation detection: leaderEpoch in ConsumerRecord and OffsetAndMetadata\n\n---\n\n### Flink's Abstraction Layer\n\n**Flink Source API (Core Concepts):**\n\n1. **Splits:** Immutable work units discovered by SplitEnumerator\n   - For Kafka: KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, startOffset, endOffset)\n   - Example: topic=\"events\", partition=0, startOffset=1000, endOffset=5000\n\n2. **SplitEnumerator:** Runs once, discovers all splits, assigns to readers\n   - Assigns splits to readers via SplitEnumeratorContext.assignSplit()\n   - Notifies completion: signalNoMoreSplits(subtaskId)\n   - Checkpoint: saves which splits are unassigned\n\n3. **SourceReader:** Runs per parallel subtask, reads assigned splits\n   - Non-blocking pollNext() method (returns InputStatus)\n   - Futures-based availability: isAvailable() \u2192 CompletableFuture<Void>\n   - Stateful: snapshotState() returns mutable state (e.g., current offset)\n\n4. **SourceReaderBase:** Helper class managing async fetch threads\n   - SplitFetcherManager: pool of fetcher threads, each with a SplitReader\n   - FutureCompletingBlockingQueue: bridges async fetch \u2192 sync poll\n   - RecordEmitter: transforms fetched elements to output type\n\n5. **RecordEmitter:** User-implemented record conversion\n   - Takes intermediate element E from SplitReader\n   - Converts to final type T and emits via SourceOutput\n   - Updates SplitState (e.g., offset) based on element\n\n---\n\n### Dual Serialization Boundary\n\n**Kafka Layer (Transport):**\n- Bytes \u2192 ConsumerRecord<K, V> via Kafka Deserializer<K>, Deserializer<V>\n- Deserializer.deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) is stateless\n- Low-level: only converts bytes to typed objects\n\n**Flink Layer (Semantic):**\n- ConsumerRecord<K, V> \u2192 custom type T via DeserializationSchema<T>\n- DeserializationSchema.deserialize(byte[] message) has access to full context\n- Optional: used for schema evolution, filtering, watermark assignment\n\n**Example Integration:**\n```java\n// Kafka deserializes: byte[] \u2192 (K key, V value)\nKafkaConsumer<String, JsonNode> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(\n    props,\n    new StringDeserializer(),\n    new JsonDeserializer()\n);\n\n// Flink's KafkaSourceReader extracts ConsumerRecord<String, JsonNode>\n// Then applies custom schema:\nnew DeserializationSchema<TradeRecord>() {\n    public TradeRecord deserialize(byte[] message) {\n        JsonNode json = mapper.readValue(message);\n        return new TradeRecord(json.get(\"id\"), json.get(\"price\"));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Checkpoint-Offset Integration Deep Dive\n\n**Phase 1: Snapshot (During Checkpoint)**\n\n```\nJobManager issues checkpoint request\n    \u2193 Barrier injected at source\nSourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext)\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls: sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 SourceReaderBase.snapshotState():\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Pauses SplitFetcherManager threads (briefly)\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Drains any buffered elements (elementsQueue)\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Calls RecordEmitter.flushState()\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500 Collects List<SplitT> with current state\n    \u2502           \u2514\u2500 For Kafka: KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, offset)\n    \u2502               where offset = highest offset processed + 1\n    \u251c\u2500 Serializes List<SplitT> using SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>\n    \u2514\u2500 Writes to ListState<byte[]> (state backend)\n    \u2193\nStateBackend (RocksDB) writes snapshot to stable storage\n    \u251c\u2500 Local: RocksDB (replica redundancy)\n    \u2514\u2500 Remote: HDFS, S3, DFS (for fault tolerance)\n    \u2193\nCheckpoint reaches operator DAG\n    \u2514\u2500 All operators snapshot state\n    \u2193\nMaster acknowledges checkpoint complete\n```\n\n**Phase 2: Commit (Post-Checkpoint)**\n\n```\nCoordinator calls: SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    \u2193\nSourceReaderBase.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n    \u251c\u2500 Extracts offsets from recent splits\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 KafkaPartitionSplit.splitId() = \"partition-X:offset-Y\"\n    \u251c\u2500 Builds: Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 TopicPartition(topic=\"events\", partition=0)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 OffsetAndMetadata(offset=5001, metadata=\"checkpoint-123\")\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ... (one entry per partition being read)\n    \u2514\u2500 Calls: kafkaConsumer.commitSync(offsets)\n        \u251c\u2500 Sends OffsetCommit request to broker\n        \u251c\u2500 Broker writes to __consumer_offsets topic\n        \u2514\u2500 Returns when replicated (durability guarantee)\n    \u2193\nConsumer group offset updated\n    \u2514\u2500 Next restart can resume from committed offset\n```\n\n**Phase 3: Recovery**\n\n```\nFlink TaskManager restarts (on failure)\n    \u2193\nSourceOperator.initializeState(StateInitializationContext)\n    \u251c\u2500 Restores ListState<byte[]> from state backend\n    \u251c\u2500 Deserializes: List<SplitT>\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 KafkaPartitionSplit(topic, partition, offset=5001)\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls: sourceReader.addSplits(splits)\n    \u2502   \u251c\u2500 KafkaSourceReader.addSplits():\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Creates KafkaConsumer if not exists\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Calls: consumer.assign(topicPartitions)\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Calls: consumer.seek(tp, offset)\n    \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Resumes polling from offset\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500 SourceReaderBase enqueues to internal queue\n    \u2193\nProcessing resumes from offset 5001\n    \u2514\u2500 No duplicate records (offset 5001 was not yet emitted before failure)\n```\n\n**Why This Works:**\n1. **Snapshots before emit:** The offset in the snapshot is the next-to-read offset (not yet emitted)\n2. **No double-counting:** If a record at offset 5000 was fetched but not emitted before failure, it's re-emitted after recovery\n3. **Atomic commits:** Kafka's offset commit is atomic per partition; commit happens after checkpoint complete\n4. **Idempotent processing:** Downstream operators must handle duplicate records (or use dedup)\n\n---\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka Side:**\n- **Producer:** User thread calls send() (async) or get() (sync); NetworkClient thread sends batches\n- **Consumer:** User thread calls poll() (blocking); Fetcher thread pre-fetches in background\n\n**Flink Source Side:**\n- **Main task thread:** Calls SourceOperator.emitNext() \u2192 SourceReader.pollNext()\n- **SplitFetcher threads:** SplitReader.fetch() (may block on I/O)\n- **Handoff via queue:** FutureCompletingBlockingQueue bridges async fetcher \u2192 sync main thread\n\n**Synchronization Points:**\n- Checkpoint barrier synchronizes across all operators\n- SourceReaderBase pauses fetcher threads during snapshotState()\n- RecordEmitter processes records before emitting (timestamp assignment, watermarks)\n\n---\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\n**Kafka's GroupCoordinator:**\n1. Each consumer sends heartbeat (session.timeout.ms)\n2. If no heartbeat for timeout, consumer marked dead\n3. Rebalance triggered: ConsumerRebalanceListener callbacks\n4. PartitionAssignor (e.g., RangeAssignor) distributes partitions\n\n**Flink's Approach:**\n- KafkaSourceReader participates in consumer group if enabled\n- If partitions revoked: reader pauses polling\n- If partitions assigned: reader resumes from committed offset\n- Seamless for single-job reading; careful for multi-job consumer groups\n\n---\n\n### Capital Markets Use Case\n\nIn a capital markets trade ingestion pipeline:\n\n1. **Producer Side:**\n   - Exchange systems produce ProducerRecord<String, TradeMsg> with timestamp=exchange time\n   - Serializer converts TradeMsg (POJO) \u2192 JSON or Avro bytes\n   - KafkaProducer batches trades, sends with acks=all for durability\n   - Topic partitioned by symbol: \"AAPL\", \"MSFT\", \"GOOG\" \u2192 partition 0, 1, 2\n\n2. **Consumer Side (Flink):**\n   - KafkaSource reads all partitions\n   - SplitEnumerator creates: KafkaPartitionSplit(\"trades\", 0), KafkaPartitionSplit(\"trades\", 1), ...\n   - SplitEnumerator assigns: SourceReader 0 gets partitions 0-2, SourceReader 1 gets partitions 3-5\n   - KafkaSourceReader wraps KafkaConsumer<String, TradeMsg>\n   - Deserializer converts JSON \u2192 TradeMsg POJO\n   - RecordEmitter extracts timestamp, assigns watermark (Watermark(tradeMsg.timestamp()))\n\n3. **Checkpoint-Offset:**\n   - Every 60s: snapshotState() saves offset per partition\n   - After checkpoint: commitSync() writes to Kafka __consumer_offsets\n   - On restart: resume from last committed offset\n   - Exactly-once guarantee: no trades lost, no duplicates within Flink (downstream dedup for cross-system failures)\n\n4. **Risk Calculation:**\n   - Downstream operators read from KafkaSourceReader output\n   - Windowed aggregation (e.g., per-symbol volume in last minute)\n   - Watermark drives window closure\n   - Late trades dropped or side-output based on policy\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  KAFKA BROKERS                                              \u2502\n\u2502  [Topic \"trades\" Partitions 0,1,2,...]                      \u2502\n\u2502  [__consumer_offsets (internal compacted topic)]            \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u2191 Fetch / Commit offsets\n                 \u2193 (poll &  KAFKA CLIENT LIBRARY (Client API)                          \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Deserializer<V>                        \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 ConsumerRecord<K, V>                                    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 OffsetAndMetadata                                       \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u2191 wraps\n                 \u2193\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  FLINK KAFKA CONNECTOR (apache/flink-connector-kafka)       \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502          \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Wraps KafkaConsumer                                     \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Deserializer bridge (Kafka \u2192 Flink types)               \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Offset tracking per partition                 \u2191 implements\n Summary\n\nThe Kafka-Flink streaming integration is a **three-layer architecture**:\n\n1. **Kafka Layer (Transport):** Produces/consumes bytes, manages replication, coordinates consumer groups, persists offsets.\n\n2. **Flink Connector Layer (Bridge):** KafkaSource/KafkaSourceReader wraps KafkaConsumer, discovers partitions as splits, maps Kafka's offset model to Flink's split+state model, applies custom deserialization.\n\n3. **Flink Core Layer (Semantics):** SourceReader/SplitEnumerator abstract the external system; SourceOperator integrates with Flink's checkpoint protocol; RecordEmitter transforms data and assigns timestamps/watermarks.\n\n**Critical Integration Point:** The checkpoint-to-offset commit flow ensures exactly-once semantics. SourceOperator.snapshotState() calls SourceReader.snapshotState(), which KafkaSourceReader translates to Kafka partition offsets. After checkpoint completion, notifyCheckpointComplete() triggers commitSync() to persist offsets to Kafka's __consumer_offsets topic. Recovery restores splits from state, seeks KafkaConsumer to those offsets, and resumes. This pattern is reusable for any external system (S3, databases, message queues) by implementing the SourceReader/SplitEnumerator interfaces.\n",

(2) Flink connector layer (apache/flink-connector-kafka) wraps KafkaConsumer, discovers partitions as SplitEnumerator splits, implements SplitReader to call consumer.poll(), maps Kafka offsets to Flink split state. (3) Flink core layer provides SourceReader/SplitEnumerator abstraction, SourceReaderBase helper with SplitFetcherManager for async fetching, RecordEmitter for timestamp/watermark assignment, SourceOperator for checkpoint integration. The checkpoint-offset integration is critical: SourceOperator.snapshotState() calls SourceReader.snapshotState() which returns List<SplitT> containing current offsets; after checkpoint completes, notifyCheckpointComplete() triggers Consumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>) to persist offsets. On recovery, splits are restored and KafkaConsumer.seek() resumes from committed offset. This pattern provides exactly-once semantics: snapshot = next-to-read offset, barrier prevents duplicates in Flink, commit after barrier ensures no re-processing. Dual serialization boundary: Kafka Deserializer<K>/Deserializer<V> converts bytes to typed objects (K, V); Flink DeserializationSchema<T> optionally wraps ConsumerRecord<K,V> for semantic transformation. Thread architecture: SplitFetcherManager runs fetcher threads calling SplitReader.fetch() (blocking on I/O), results enqueued to FutureCompletingBlockingQueue, main task thread calls SourceReader.pollNext() (non-blocking) to drain queue and emit records via RecordEmitter.\\\"\\n  }\\n}\\n",

Non-blocking poll loop: fetcher threads push RecordsWithSplitIds \u2192 queue, main thread pulls and calls emitRecord().\\\"\\n      },\\n      {\\n        \\\"path\\\": \\\"flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java\\\",\\n        \\\"repo\\\": \\\"github.com/apache/flink\\\",\\n        \\\"description\\\": \\\"Interface for reading from splits: fetch() \u2192 RecordsWithSplitIds<E> (may block on I/O), handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT>) (non-blocking), wakeUp() (interrupt blocking fetch), pauseOrResumeSplits(Collection<SplitT>, Collection<SplitT>). Transforms intermediate element E (from SplitReader) to final type T, emits via SourceOutput (collects with timestamp/watermark), updates mutable split state (e.g., offset tracking).\\\"\\n      },\\n      {\\n        \\\"path\\\": \\\"flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java\\\",\\n        \\\"repo\\\": \\\"github.com/apache/flink\\\",\\n        \\\"description\\\": \\\"Flink serde boundary interface: open(InitializationContext), deserialize(byte[] message) \u2192 T, deserialize(byte[], Collector<T> out), isEndOfStream(T) \u2192 boolean. Key methods: snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext) calls sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) and writes to ListState<byte[]>; notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId) triggers offset commits; initializeState() restores splits and calls addSplits(); emitNext() polls sourceReader. Integrates with checkpoint protocol for exactly-once semantics.\\\"\\n      }\\n    ],\\n    \\\"reasoning\\\": \\\"The Kafka-Flink architecture spans three layers: (1) Kafka transport layer provides ProducerRecord/ConsumerRecord data structures, Serializer/Deserializer interfaces for bytes conversion, Consumer.commitSync() for durable offset commits to __consumer_offsets topic. (2) Flink connector layer (apache/flink-connector-kafka) wraps KafkaConsumer, discovers partitions as SplitEnumerator splits, implements SplitReader to call consumer.poll(), maps Kafka offsets to Flink split state. (3) Flink core layer provides SourceReader/SplitEnumerator abstraction, SourceReaderBase helper with SplitFetcherManager for async fetching, RecordEmitter for timestamp/watermark assignment, SourceOperator for checkpoint integration. The checkpoint-offset integration is critical: SourceOperator.snapshotState() calls SourceReader.snapshotState() which returns List<SplitT> containing current offsets; after checkpoint completes, notifyCheckpointComplete() triggers Consumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>) to persist offsets. On recovery, splits are restored and KafkaConsumer.seek() resumes from committed offset. This pattern provides exactly-once semantics: snapshot = next-to-read offset, barrier prevents duplicates in Flink, commit after barrier ensures no re-processing. Dual serialization boundary: Kafka Deserializer<K>/Deserializer<V> converts bytes to typed objects (K, V); Flink DeserializationSchema<T> optionally wraps ConsumerRecord<K,V> for semantic transformation. Thread architecture: SplitFetcherManager runs fetcher threads calling SplitReader.fetch() (blocking on I/O), results enqueued to FutureCompletingBlockingQueue, main task thread calls SourceReader.pollNext() (non-blocking) to drain queue and emit records via RecordEmitter.\\\"\\n  }\\n}\\n",

# Kafka-Flink Streaming Data Flow Architecture Analysis

## Files Examined

### Apache Kafka (github.com/sg-benchmarks/kafka--be816b82)

**Producer API:**
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/Producer.java` — Interface for KafkaProducer with send(), flush(), and transactional methods
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java` — Implementation of Producer<K,V> with networking, batching, and compression
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerRecord.java` — Data structure for topic, partition, key, value, timestamp, headers
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Serializer.java` — Interface: serialize(String topic, T data) → byte[]

**Consumer API:**
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java` — Interface for KafkaConsumer with subscribe(), poll(), commitSync(), seek(), position()
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java` — Implementation with consumer group coordination, rebalancing, offset management
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/ConsumerRecord.java` — Data structure for topic, partition, offset, key, value, timestamp, headers
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java` — Interface: deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) → T
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/OffsetAndMetadata.java` — Wraps offset + optional metadata for commit operations (commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>))
